<p><b>Arunachal Pradesh</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɑːr/ 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/tʃ/ 'ch' in 'china'">tʃ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="/ʃ/ 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span></span>/</a></span></span> is one of the twenty-nine states of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Located in <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" title="Northeast India">northeast India</a>, it holds the most north-eastern position among the states in the north-east region of India. Arunachal Pradesh borders the states of <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a> to the south, and shares international borders with <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> in the east and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in the north. <a href="/wiki/Itanagar" title="Itanagar">Itanagar</a> is the capital of the state. Arunachal Pradesh has territorial disputes with both the <a href="/wiki/Two_Chinas" title="Two Chinas">PRC and ROC</a> due to its cultural, ethnic and geographic proximity to Tibet.</p>
<p>A major part of the state, formerly called the <a href="/wiki/North-East_Frontier_Agency" title="North-East Frontier Agency">North-East Frontier Agency</a>, is disputed by <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> as the legality of the <a href="/wiki/Simla_Accord_(1914)" title="Simla Accord (1914)">Simla Accord</a> is not recognized by it. China <a href="/wiki/Sino-Indian_border_dispute" title="Sino-Indian border dispute">claims most of the state</a> as <a href="/wiki/South_Tibet" title="South Tibet">South Tibet</a>. The state is seen to have major potential for <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wirsing_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wirsing-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh, whose name means <i>Land of the Dawn-Lit Mountains</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, is also known as the <i>Orchid State of India</i> or the <i>Paradise of the Botanists</i>. Geographically, it is the largest among the North-east Indian states commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Sister_States" title="Seven Sister States">Seven Sister States</a>. As in other parts of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" title="Northeast India">Northeast India</a>, the people native to the state trace their origins to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman" title="Tibeto-Burman">Tibeto-Burman</a> people. In recent times, large number of migrants from various parts of India and other lands have built extensive economic and cultural ties with the state's population.</p>
<p>No reliable population count of the migrant population exists, and the percentage estimating the total actual population accordingly, vary. Arunachal Pradesh has the highest number of regional languages in the Indian subcontinent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> enriched with diverse culture and traditions.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> tools found in Arunachal Pradesh indicate that people have been living in the Himalayan region for at least eleven thousand years. The earliest inhabitants of Bhutan and adjoining Himalayan areas of South Asia were the people from <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">Indus Valley Civilisation</a>, whose history predates the onset of <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> in South Asia around 3300BC before the coming of other ethnic groups from <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_China" title="South China">South China</a> some 2,000 years ago.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The history of pre-modern Arunachal Pradesh is unclear. Oral histories possessed to this day by many Arunachali tribes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman" title="Tibeto-Burman">Tibeto-Burman</a> stock are much richer and point unambiguously to a northern origin in modern-day Tibet. Again corroboration remains difficult. From the point of view of material culture it is clear that most indigenous Arunachali groups align with Burma-area hill tribals, a fact that could either be explainable in terms of a northern Burmese origin or from westward cultural diffusion.</p>
<p>According to the Arunachal Pradesh government, the Hindu texts <a href="/wiki/Kalika_Purana" title="Kalika Purana">Kalika Purana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a> mention the region as the Prabhu Mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Puranas" title="Puranas">Puranas</a>, and where sage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parashuram" title="Parashuram">Parashuram</a> washed away sins, the sage <a href="/wiki/Vyasa" title="Vyasa">Vyasa</a> meditated, King <a href="/wiki/Bhishmaka" title="Bhishmaka">Bhishmaka</a> founded his kingdom, and Lord <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> married his consort <a href="/wiki/Rukmini" title="Rukmini">Rukmini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recorded history from an outside perspective only became available in the <a href="/wiki/Ahom_language" title="Ahom language">Ahom</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sutiya_people" title="Sutiya people">Sutiya</a> chronicles. The <a href="/wiki/Monpa_people" title="Monpa people">Monpa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherdukpen" title="Sherdukpen">Sherdukpen</a> do keep historical records of the existence of local chiefdoms in the northwest as well. Northwestern parts of this area came under the control of the Monpa kingdom of Monyul, which flourished between 500 B.C. and 600 A.D. This region then came under the loose control of <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>, especially in the Northern areas. The remaining parts of the state, especially those bordering <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, were under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Sutiya_Kingdom" title="Sutiya Kingdom">Sutiya Kings</a> until the Ahom-Sutiya battle in the 16th century. The <a href="/wiki/Ahom_people" title="Ahom people">Ahoms</a> held the areas until the annexation of India by the British in 1858. However, most Arunachali tribes remained in practice largely autonomous up until Indian independence and the formalisation of indigenous administration in 1947.</p>
<p>Recent excavations of ruins of Hindu temples such as the 14th century Malinithan at the foot of the Siang hills in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Siang" title="West Siang">West Siang</a> were built during the <a href="/wiki/Sutiya_Kingdom" title="Sutiya Kingdom">Sutiya reign</a>. Another notable heritage site, Bhismaknagar, has led to suggestions that the Idu (<a href="/wiki/Mishmi_people" title="Mishmi people">Mishmi</a>) had an advanced culture and administration in prehistoric times. Again, however, no evidence directly associates Bhismaknagar with this or any other known culture but the <a href="/wiki/Sutiya_Kingdom" title="Sutiya Kingdom">Sutiya rulers</a> held the areas around Bhismaknagar from the 12th to 16th century. The third heritage site, the 400-year-old <a href="/wiki/Tawang_Monastery" title="Tawang Monastery">Tawang Monastery</a> in the extreme north-west of the state, provides some historical evidence of the Buddhist tribal people. The sixth <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsangyang_Gyatso,_6th_Dalai_Lama" title="Tsangyang Gyatso, 6th Dalai Lama">Tsangyang Gyatso</a> was born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tawang_Town" title="Tawang Town">Tawang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drawing_of_McMahon_line">Drawing of McMahon line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Drawing of McMahon line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1223" data-file-width="1498" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/220px-British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/330px-British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/440px-British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Indian_Empire_1909_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British map published in 1909 showing the Indo-Tibetan traditional border (<i>eastern section, top right</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3449" data-file-width="3729" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/220px-1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/330px-1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg/440px-1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1922_Map_of_India_by_Bartholomew_in_Imperial_Gazetteer_of_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British map published in 1922 shows an Indo-Bhutan-Tibetan border different from the 1909 map.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1913–1914 representatives of China, Tibet and Britain met in India ending with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simla_Accord_(1913)" title="Simla Accord (1913)">Simla Accord</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> However, the Chinese representatives refused the territory negotiation. This treaty's objective was to define the borders between Inner and Outer Tibet as well as between Outer Tibet and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>. British administrator, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Henry_McMahon" title="Sir Henry McMahon">Sir Henry McMahon</a>, drew up the 550 miles (890 km) <a href="/wiki/McMahon_Line" title="McMahon Line">McMahon Line</a> as the border between British India and Outer Tibet during the Simla Conference. The Tibetan and British representatives at the conference agreed to the line, and Tibet ceded <a href="/wiki/Tawang" title="Tawang">Tawang</a> and other Tibetan areas to the British Empire. Thus, the Chinese representative refused to accept the agreement and walked out.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="2009-02-26 (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Tibetan and British governments went ahead with the <a href="/wiki/Simla_Accord_(1914)" title="Simla Accord (1914)">Simla Agreement</a> and declared that the benefits of other articles of this treaty would not be bestowed on China as long as it stays out of the purview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The Chinese position was that Tibet was not independent from China: Tibet could not have independently signed treaties, and per the Anglo-Chinese (1906) and Anglo-Russian (1907) conventions, any such agreement was invalid without Chinese assent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-int_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-int-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Simla was initially rejected by the Government of India as incompatible with the 1907 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Convention" title="Anglo-Russian Convention">Anglo-Russian Convention</a>. This agreement (Anglo-Russian Convention) was renounced by Russia and Britain jointly in 1921. However, with the collapse of Chinese power in Tibet, the line had no serious challenges as <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> had signed the convention. Therefore, it was forgotten to the extent that no new maps were published until 1935, when civil service officer <a href="/wiki/Olaf_Caroe" title="Olaf Caroe">Olaf Caroe</a> called attention to this issue. The <a href="/wiki/Survey_of_India" title="Survey of India">Survey of India</a> published a map showing the McMahon Line as the official boundary in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ray2007_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ray2007-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1938, the British finally published the Simla Convention as a bilateral accord two decades after the Simla Conference; in 1938 the Survey of India published a detailed map showing Tawang as part of <a href="/wiki/North-East_Frontier_Agency" title="North-East Frontier Agency">North-East Frontier Agency</a>. In 1944 Britain established administrations in the area from Dirang Dzong in the west to <a href="/wiki/Walong" title="Walong">Walong</a> in the east. Tibet altered its position on the McMahon Line in late 1947 when the Tibetan government wrote a note presented to the newly independent Indian Ministry of External Affairs laying claims to Tawang south of the McMahon Line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The situation developed further as India became independent in 1947 and the People's Republic of China (PRC) was established in 1949. In November 1950, with the PRC poised to take over Tibet, India unilaterally declared that the McMahon Line is the boundary — and, in 1951, forced the last remnants of Tibetan administration out of the Tawang area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The PRC has never recognised the McMahon Line and claims Tawang on behalf of Tibetans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">14th Dalai Lama</a>, who led the Tibetan government from 1950 to 1959, was quoted in 2003 as saying that Tawang was "actually part of the Tibetan administration" before the Simla Accord.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpt_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-tpt-23">[23]</a></sup> He clarified his position in 2008, saying that as far as Tibet was concerned "Tawang is part of India".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpt_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-tpt-23">[23]</a></sup> According to the Dalai Lama, "In 1962 during the India-China war, the People's Liberation Army (PLA) already occupied all these areas (Arunachal Pradesh) but they announced a unilateral ceasefire and withdrew, accepting the current international boundary".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sino-Indian_War">Sino-Indian War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sino-Indian War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sino-Indian_War" title="Sino-Indian War">Sino-Indian War</a></div>
<p>The NEFA (<a href="/wiki/North-East_Frontier_Agency" title="North-East Frontier Agency">North-East Frontier Agency</a>) was created in 1954. The issue was quiet for nearly a decade, a period of cordial Sino-Indian relations, but the re-emergence of the issue was a major cause of the Sino-Indian War of 1962. The cause of the escalation into war is still disputed by both Chinese and Indian sources. During the war in 1962, the PRC captured most area of Arunachal Pradesh. However, China soon declared victory, voluntarily withdrew back to the <a href="/wiki/McMahon_Line" title="McMahon Line">McMahon Line</a> and returned Indian prisoners of war in 1963. The war resulted in the termination of <a href="/wiki/Barter" title="Barter">barter</a> trade with Tibet, although in 2007 the state government has shown signs to resume barter trade with Tibet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tawang">Tawang</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tawang">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tawang_Monastery_(Tibetan_Buddhist).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3564" data-file-width="5346" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg/220px-Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg/330px-Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg/440px-Tawang_Monastery_%28Tibetan_Buddhist%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tawang_Monastery_(Tibetan_Buddhist).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tawang Monastery (Tibetan Buddhist)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In recent years, China has occasionally made statements in conjunction with its claims on Tawang. India has rebutted these claims by the Chinese government and the Indian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> has informed the Chinese government that Tawang is an integral part of India. India reiterated this to the Chinese prime minister when the two prime ministers met in Thailand in October 2009. It was reported that during 2016, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Army" title="Chinese Army">Chinese Army</a> had briefly invaded Arunachal Pradesh. This was refuted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_for_Home_Affairs" title="Minister of State for Home Affairs">Minister of State for Home Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiren_Rijiju" title="Kiren Rijiju">Kiren Rijiju</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>China objected to the visit of the <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> to Tawang in November 2009 though the Dalai Lama had previously visited Tawang several times since he fled from Tibet in 1959. India rejected the Chinese objection and said that the Dalai Lama is an honoured guest in India and could visit any place in India. The Dalai Lama visited Tawang on 8 November 2009. About 30,000 people including those from neighbouring countries, Nepal and Bhutan, attended his religious discourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was received and welcomed by the Chief Minister of Arunachal Pradesh and the people of Arunachal Pradesh. The residents of Tawang painted their houses and decorated the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_name">Current name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Current name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>NEFA was renamed as Arunachal Pradesh by Late Sri Bibhabasu Das Shastri, then the director of research, on 20 January 1972 and it became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Territory" title="Union Territory">Union Territory</a>. Arunachal Pradesh became a state on 20 February 1987.</p>
<p>More recently, Arunachal Pradesh has come to face threats from certain insurgent groups, notably the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Council_of_Nagaland" title="National Socialist Council of Nagaland">National Socialist Council of Nagaland</a> (NSCN), who are believed to have base camps in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Changlang_district" title="Changlang district">Changlang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tirap_district" title="Tirap district">Tirap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> There are occasional reports of these groups harassing local people and extorting protection money.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Especially along the Tibetan border, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_army" title="Indian army">Indian army</a> has a considerable presence due to concerns about Chinese intentions in the region. <a href="/wiki/Foreigners_(Protected_Areas)_Order_1958_(India)" title="Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order 1958 (India)">Special permits</a> called <a href="/wiki/Inner_Line_Permit" title="Inner Line Permit">Inner Line Permits</a> (ILP) are required to enter Arunachal Pradesh through any of its checkgates on the border with <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg/220px-Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg/330px-Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg/440px-Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mountains_of_Arunachal_Pradesh.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A lake at <a href="/wiki/Sela_Pass" title="Sela Pass">Sela</a> on the way to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tawang_Town" title="Tawang Town">Tawang</a> in West Kameng district of Arunachal Pradesh.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salna_Bari_,_Bhalukpong.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="720" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg/220px-Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg/330px-Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg/440px-Salna_Bari_%2C_Bhalukpong.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salna_Bari_,_Bhalukpong.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view from <a href="/wiki/Bhalukpong" title="Bhalukpong">Bhalukpong</a>, a small town by the southern reaches of the Himalayas.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh is located between 26.28° N and 29.30° N latitude and 91.20° E and 97.30° E longitude and has 83,743 square kilometre area.</p>
<p>Most of Arunachal Pradesh is covered by the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>. However, parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lohit_District" title="Lohit District">Lohit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Changlang" title="Changlang">Changlang</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tirap_District" title="Tirap District">Tirap</a> are covered by the <a href="/wiki/Patkai" title="Patkai">Patkai</a> hills. Kangto, Nyegi Kangsang, the main Gorichen peak and the Eastern Gorichen peak are some of the highest peaks in this region of the Himalayas. The land is mostly mountainous with the Himalayan ranges running north south. These divide the state into five river valleys: the Kameng, the Subansiri, the Siang, the Lohit and the Tirap. All these are fed by snow from the Himalayas and countless rivers and rivulets. The mightiest of these rivers is Siang, called the Tsangpo in Tibet, which becomes the Brahmaputra after it is joined by the Dibang and the Lohit in the plains of Assam.</p>
<p>The Himalayan ranges that extend up to the eastern Arunachal separate it from Tibet. The ranges extend toward Nagaland, and form a boundary between India and Burma in Changlang and Tirap district, acting as a natural barrier called Patkai Bum Hills. They are low mountains compared to the Greater Himalayas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of Arunachal Pradesh varies with elevation. Areas that are at a very high elevation in the Upper Himalaya close to the Tibetan border have an alpine or <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> climate. Below the Upper Himalayas are the Middle Himalayas, where people experience a temperate climate. Areas at the sub-Himalayan and sea-level elevation generally experience humid, sub-tropical climate with hot summers and mild winters.</p>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh receives heavy rainfall of 2,000 to 4,100 millimetres (79 to 161 in) annually, most of it between May and September. The mountain slopes and hills are covered with alpine, temperate, and subtropical forests of dwarf <a href="/wiki/Rhododendron" title="Rhododendron">rhododendron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maple" title="Maple">maple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">fir</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sal_tree" title="Sal tree">sal</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Shorea_robusta" title="Shorea robusta">Shorea robusta</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Teak" title="Teak">teak</a> are the main economically valuable species.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bio-geographically it lies in the Eastern Himalayan province, the richest biogeographical province of the Himalayan zone which is also classified as the biodiversity hotspot. Arunachal Pradesh is endowed with diverse forests and magnificent wildlife. It harbors over 5000 plants, about 85 terrestrial mammals, over 500 birds and a large number of butterflies, insects and reptiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> At the lowest elevations, essentially at Arunachal Pradesh's border with <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Brahmaputra_Valley_semi-evergreen_forests" title="Brahmaputra Valley semi-evergreen forests">Brahmaputra Valley semi-evergreen forests</a>. Much of the state, including the Himalayan foothills and the Patkai hills, are home to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_broadleaf_forests" title="Eastern Himalayan broadleaf forests">Eastern Himalayan broadleaf forests</a>. Toward the northern border with Tibet, with increasing elevation, come a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_subalpine_conifer_forests" title="Eastern Himalayan subalpine conifer forests">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Himalayan_subalpine_conifer_forests" title="Northeastern Himalayan subalpine conifer forests">Northeastern Himalayan subalpine conifer forests</a> followed by <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_alpine_shrub_and_meadows" title="Eastern Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows">Eastern Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows</a> and ultimately rock and ice on the highest peaks. It supports a large number of medicinal plants and within Ziro valley of Lower Subansiri district 158 medicinal plants are being used by its inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_by_GDP" title="List of Indian states by GDP">List of Indian states by GDP</a></div>
<p>The chart below displays the trend of the gross state domestic product of Arunachal Pradesh at market prices by the Ministry of Statistics and Programme Implementation with figures in billions of Indian Rupees.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<p>Arunachal Pradesh's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross state domestic product</a> was estimated at US$706 million at current prices in 2004 and US$1.75 billion at current prices in 2012. Agriculture primarily drives the economy. Jhum, the local term used for shifting cultivation is being widely practised among the tribal groups, though owing to the gradual growth of other sources of income in the recent years, it is not being practised as prominently as it was earlier. Arunachal Pradesh has close to 61,000 square kilometres of forests, and forest products are the next most significant sector of the economy. Among the crops grown here are rice, maize, millet, wheat, pulses, sugarcane, ginger, and oilseeds. Arunachal is also ideal for horticulture and fruit orchards. Its major industries are rice mills, fruit preservation and processing units, and handloom handicrafts. <a href="/wiki/Sawmill" title="Sawmill">Sawmills</a> and plywood trades are prohibited under law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> There are many saw mills in AP. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh accounts for a large percentage share of India's untapped hydroelectric potential. In 2008, the government of Arunachal Pradesh signed numerous memorandum of understanding with various companies planning some 42 hydroelectric schemes that will produce electricity in excess of 27,000 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Siang_Hydroelectric_Project" title="Upper Siang Hydroelectric Project">Upper Siang Hydroelectric Project</a>, which is expected to generate between 10,000 and 12,000 MW, began in April 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_North_East_India" title="Tourism in North East India">Tourism in North East India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg/220px-Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg/330px-Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg/440px-Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Birsa_Munda_Waterfall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Birsa Munda Waterfall</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mehao_Lake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mehao_Lake.jpg/220px-Mehao_Lake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mehao_Lake.jpg/330px-Mehao_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Mehao_Lake.jpg/440px-Mehao_Lake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mehao_Lake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mehao Lake</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state, on account of its unrivalled aesthetics and diverse cultural heritage possesses a great tourism potential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Popular tourist attractions include <a href="/wiki/Tawang" title="Tawang">Tawang</a> (a town with a Buddhist monastery) at 3000 m elevation, <a href="/wiki/Ziro" title="Ziro">Ziro</a> (which holds cultural festivals),Yomcha (limestone caves called 'tapen uru'), the Namdapha tiger project in <a href="/wiki/Changlang" title="Changlang">Changlang</a> district and Sela lake near <a href="/wiki/Bomdila" title="Bomdila">Bomdila</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a> bridges overhanging the river. Religious places of interest include Malinithan in Lekhabali, Rukhmininagar near <a href="/wiki/Roing" title="Roing">Roing</a> (the place as per the popular Hindu mythology, Rukmini, Lord Krishna's wife, said to have lived), and <a href="/wiki/Parshuram_Kund" title="Parshuram Kund">Parshuram Kund</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lohit_district" title="Lohit district">Lohit district</a> as <a href="/wiki/Puranas" title="Puranas">Puranas</a> is the lake where sage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parshuram" title="Parshuram">Parshuram</a> washed away his sins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The Ganga lake(Gyaker sinyi or Gekar Sinyi)and various other tourist hot spots.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_(photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="1500" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg/220px-Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg/330px-Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg/440px-Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_%28photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Pagoda_in_Arunachal_Pradesh_(photo_-_Jim_Ankan_Deka).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Golden Pagoda at Namsai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state provides abundant scope for angling, boating, rafting, trekking and hiking. Rafting and trekking are common activities. Some suggested routes for travel or trekking are</p>
<ul>
<li>Tezpur–Tipi–Bomdila-Tawang-se la pass</li>
<li>Tinsukia–Tezu-Parasuramkund</li>
<li>Margherita–Miao-Namdapha</li>
<li>Itanagar–Ziro-Daporijo–Along (or Aalo)-pandighat.</li>
<li>Aalo – Yomcha (52 km)</li>
</ul>
<p>Over the years, the <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Museum,_Itanagar" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Museum, Itanagar">Jawaharlal Nehru Museum, Itanagar</a> has become an important tourist destination in the state capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ita_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ita-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Golden Pagoda Monastery at Namsai is another tourist attraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state is rich in wildlife and has a number of wildlife sanctuaries and national parks with rare animals, birds and plants. Perhaps the highest diversity of mammals in India is in Arunachal Pradesh (200+ species).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The diversity of birds is also very high, 700+ and is second only to <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Demographics of Arunachal Pradesh">Demographics of Arunachal Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="692" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg/220px-Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg/330px-Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg/440px-Nishi_tribal_from_Arunachal_-_Diganta_Talukdar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<p>Arunachal Pradesh can be roughly divided into a set of semi-distinct cultural spheres, on the basis of tribal identity, language, religion and material culture: the Tibetic area bordering <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> in the west, the Tani area in the centre of the state, the Mishmi area to the east of the Tani area, the <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singpho_people" title="Singpho people">Singpho</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangsa" title="Tangsa">Tangsa</a> area bordering Myanmar, and the "<a href="/wiki/Naga_people" title="Naga people">Naga</a>" area to the south, which also borders Myanmar. In between there are transition zones, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aka_(tribe)" title="Aka (tribe)">Aka</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hruso_people" title="Hruso people">Hruso</a>/<a href="/wiki/Miji_people" title="Miji people">Miji</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherdukpen" title="Sherdukpen">Sherdukpen</a> area, which provides a "buffer" of sorts between the Tibetic Buddhist tribes and the animist <a href="/wiki/Tani_(tribes)" title="Tani (tribes)">Tani hill tribes</a>. In addition, there are isolated peoples scattered throughout the state, such as the Sulung.</p>
<p>Within each of these cultural spheres, one finds populations of related tribes speaking related languages and sharing similar traditions. In the Tibetic area, one finds large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Monpa_people" title="Monpa people">Monpa</a> tribespeople, with several subtribes speaking closely related but mutually incomprehensible languages, and also large numbers of Tibetan refugees. Within the Tani area, major tribes include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nyishi_people" title="Nyishi people">Nyishi</a>, which many people have recently come to apply to encompass the derogatory words; like dafla &amp; Hills Miri. <a href="/wiki/Apatani_people" title="Apatani people">Apatani</a> also live among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nyishi_people" title="Nyishi people">Nyishi</a>, but are distinct. In the centre, one finds predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galo_people" title="Galo people">Galo people</a>, with the major sub-groups of Karka, Lodu, Bogum, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lare" title="Lare">Lare</a> and Pugo among others, extending to the <a href="/wiki/Ramo" title="Ramo">Ramo</a> and Pailibo areas (which are close in many ways to Galo). In the east, one finds the <a href="/wiki/Adi_people" title="Adi people">Adi</a> with many subtribes including <a href="/wiki/Padam_tribe" title="Padam tribe">Padam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dusadh" title="Dusadh">Pasi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minyong" title="Minyong">Minyong</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bokar" title="Bokar">Bokar</a>, among others. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milang" title="Milang">Milang</a>, while also falling within the general "Adi" sphere, are in many ways quite distinct. Moving east, the Idu, Miju and Digaru make up the "Mishmi" cultural-linguistic area, which may or may not form a coherent historical grouping.</p>
<p>Moving southeast, the <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai</a> <a href="/wiki/Khamti_people" title="Khamti people">Khamti</a> are linguistically distinct from their neighbours and culturally distinct from the majority of other Arunachalese tribes. They follow the Theravada∞ sect of Buddhism. They also exhibit considerable convergence with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singpho_people" title="Singpho people">Singpho</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangsa" title="Tangsa">Tangsa</a> tribes of the same area, all of which are also found in Burma. Besides, the <a href="/wiki/Nocte_language" title="Nocte language">Nocte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wancho_language" title="Wancho language">Wancho</a> exhibit cultural and possibly also linguistic affinities to the tribes of <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a>, which they border.</p>
<p>In addition, there are large numbers of migrants from Bangladesh, who, while legally not entitled to settle permanently, in practice stay indefinitely, progressively altering the traditional demographic makeup of the state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BuddhaTwang.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="800" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/BuddhaTwang.jpg/250px-BuddhaTwang.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/BuddhaTwang.jpg/375px-BuddhaTwang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/BuddhaTwang.jpg/500px-BuddhaTwang.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BuddhaTwang.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> is practised by 13% of the population. Shown here is a statue of <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">the Buddha</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tawang" title="Tawang">Tawang</a>, Arunachal Pradesh.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Literacy has risen in official figures to 66.95% in 2011 from 54.74% in 2001. The literate population is said to number 789,943. The number of literate males is 454,532 (73.69%) and the number of literate females is 335,411 (59.57%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Religion in Arunachal Pradesh">Religion in Arunachal Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (1.9%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DeepPink; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other (0.84%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An uncertain but relatively large percentage of Arunachal's population are nature worshippers (indigenous religions), and follow their own distinct traditional institutions like the Nyedar Namlo by the Nyishi, the Rangfrah by the Tangsa &amp; Nocte, Medar Melo by the Apatani, the Kargu Gamgi by the Galo and Donyi-Polo Dere by the Adi under the umbrella of the indigenous religion the Donyi-Polo. A small number of Arunachali people have traditionally identified as <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a>, although the number is growing as animist traditions are merged with Hindu traditions. <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> predominates in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Tawang" title="Tawang">Tawang</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Kameng" title="West Kameng">West Kameng</a>, and isolated regions adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism" title="Theravada Buddhism">Theravada Buddhism</a> is practised by groups living near the Burmese border. Around 30% of the population are followers of the Christian faith.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2011 Indian Census, the religions of Arunachal Pradesh break down as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Christian: 418,732 (30.26%)</li>
<li>Hindu: 401,876 (29.04%)</li>
<li>Others (mostly <a href="/wiki/Donyi-Polo" title="Donyi-Polo">Donyi-Polo</a>): 362,553 (26.2%)</li>
<li>Buddhist: 162,815 (11.76%)</li>
<li>Muslim: 27,045 (1.9%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikh</a>: 1,865 (0.1%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a>: 216 (&lt;0.1%)</li>
</ul>
<p>As per 2001 census, out of the 705,158 tribals living in Arunachal, 333,102 are Animist (47.24%), 186,617 are Christian (26.46%), 92,577 are Hindu (13.13%), and 82,634 are Buddhist (11.72%).</p>
<p>Out of the 101 recognised tribes, 37 have an animist majority (Nyishi, Adi Gallong, <a href="/wiki/Tagin_people" title="Tagin people">Tagin</a>, Adi Minyong, Adi, <a href="/wiki/Apatani_people" title="Apatani people">Apatani</a>.etc.), 23 have a Christian majority (Wancho, Mossang Tangsa, Bori, Yobin.etc.), 15 have a Hindu majority (Mishmi, Mishing/<a href="/wiki/Hill_Miri_people" title="Hill Miri people">Miri</a>, Deori, Aka, Longchang Tangsa.etc.) and 17 have a Buddhist majority (Monpa, Khampti, Tawang Monpa, Momba, Singpho, Sherdukpen.etc.). The remaining eight tribes are multi-faith, i.e., they do not have a dominant religion (Nocte, Tangsa, Naga.etc.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
<p>Modern-day Arunachal Pradesh is one of the linguistically richest and most diverse regions in all of Asia, being home to at least 30 and possibly as many as 50 distinct languages in addition to innumerable dialects and subdialects thereof. Boundaries between languages very often correlate with tribal divisions—for example, Apatani and Nyishi are tribally and linguistically distinct—but shifts in tribal identity and alignment over time have also ensured that a certain amount of complication enters into the picture—for example, Galo is and has seemingly always been linguistically distinct from Adi, whereas the earlier tribal alignment of Galo with Adi (i.e., "Adi Gallong") has only recently been essentially dissolved.</p>
<p>The vast majority of languages indigenous to modern-day Arunachal Pradesh belong to the Paleao-Mongoloid with <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman</a> groups of language family. The majority of these in turn belong to a single branch of Tibeto-Burman, namely Abo-Tani language. Almost all <a href="/wiki/Tani_languages" title="Tani languages">Tani languages</a> are indigenous to central Arunachal Pradesh, including (moving from west to east) speak Tani language viz., the Nyishi, the Apatani, the <a href="/wiki/Tagin_people" title="Tagin people">Tagin</a>, the Galo, the Bokar, the Adi, the Padam, the Pasi, and the Minyong. The Tani language is noticeably characterised by an overall relative uniformity, suggesting relatively recent origin and dispersal within their present-day area of concentration. Most of the Tani languages are mutually intelligible with at least one other Tani language, meaning that the area constitutes a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dialect_chain" title="Dialect chain">dialect chain</a>, as was once found in much of Europe; only Apatani and Milang stand out as relatively unusual in the Tani context. Tani languages are among the better-studied languages of the region.</p>
<p>To the east of the Tani area lie three virtually undescribed and highly endangered languages of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mishmi" title="Mishmi">Mishmi</a>" group of Tibeto-Burman, <a href="/wiki/Idu_Mishmi_language" title="Idu Mishmi language">Idu</a>, Digaru and <a href="/wiki/Miju_Mishmi_tribe" title="Miju Mishmi tribe">Miju</a>. A number of speakers of these languages are also found in Tibet. The relationships of these languages, both amongst one another and to other area languages, are as yet uncertain. Further south, one finds the <a href="/wiki/Jingpho_language" title="Jingpho language">Singpho</a> (Kachin) language, which is primarily spoken by large populations in Myanmar, and the <a href="/wiki/Nocte_language" title="Nocte language">Nocte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wancho_language" title="Wancho language">Wancho languages</a>, which show affiliations to certain Naga languages spoken to the south in modern-day Nagaland.</p>
<p>To the west and north of the Tani area are found at least one and possibly as many as four Bodic languages, including Dakpa and Tshangla; within modern-day India, these languages go by the cognate but, in usage, distinct designations <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monpa_language" title="Monpa language">Monpa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memba" title="Memba">Memba</a>. Most speakers of these languages or closely related Bodic languages are found in neighbouring Bhutan and Tibet, and Monpa and Memba populations remain closely adjacent to these border regions.</p>
<p>Between the Bodic and Tani areas lie a large number of almost completely undescribed and unclassified languages, which, speculatively considered Tibeto-Burman, exhibit many unique structural and lexical properties that probably reflect both a long history in the region and a complex history of language contact with neighbouring populations. Among them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherdukpen" title="Sherdukpen">Sherdukpen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bugun" title="Bugun">Bugun</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aka_(tribe)" title="Aka (tribe)">Aka</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hruso_languages" title="Hruso languages">Hruso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koro_language_(India)" title="Koro language (India)">Koro</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miji_language" title="Miji language">Miji</a>, Bangru and <a href="/wiki/Puroik_language" title="Puroik language">Puroik</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulung" title="Sulung">Sulung</a>. The high linguistic significance these languages is belied by the extreme paucity of documentation and description of them, even in view of their highly endangered status. Puroik, in particular, is perhaps one of the most culturally and linguistically unique and significant populations in all of Asia from proto-historical and anthropological-linguistic perspectives, and yet virtually no information of any real reliability regarding their culture or language can be found in print.</p>
<p>Finally, other then the Bodic and Tani language there is also certain migratory languages which are largely spoken by migratory and central Government employees who are serving in the state in different departments and institutions in modern-day Arunachal Pradesh. They are classified as Non-Tribal as per the provisions of the Constitution of India.</p>
<p>Outside of Tibeto-Burman, one finds in Arunachal Pradesh a single representative of the Tai languages language family, spoken by the tribe like the Khampti and Singpho which is closely affiliated to the Shan language of the Myanmar. Seemingly, Khampti is a recent arrival in Arunachal Pradesh whose presence dates from 18th and/or early 19th-century migrations from northern Burma. In addition to these non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-European" title="Indo-European">Indo-European</a> languages, the Indo-European languages <a href="/wiki/Assamese_language" title="Assamese language">Assamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, English, <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> and especially <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> are making strong inroads into Arunachal Pradesh. Primarily as a result of the primary education system—in which classes are generally taught by Hindi-speaking immigrant teachers from Bihar and other Hindi-speaking parts of northern India—a large and growing section of the population now speaks a semi-creolized variety of Hindi as its mother tongue. Despite, or perhaps because of, the linguistic diversity of the region, English is the only official language recognised in the state.</p>
<p>The speakers of major languages of the state according to the 2001 census are Nyishi (208,337), Adi (193,379), Bengali (97,149), Nepali (94,919), Hindi (81,186), Monpa (55,428), Assamese (51,551), Wancho (48,544), Tangsa (34,231), Mishmi (33,522), Mishing (33,381), Nocte (32,591), and Others (64,711).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Itanagar_Airport" title="Itanagar Airport">Itanagar Airport</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Greenfield_project" title="Greenfield project">Greenfield project</a> serving Itanagar is being planned at Holongi at a cost of Rs. 6.50 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The existing state owned <a href="/wiki/Daporijo_Airport" title="Daporijo Airport">Daporijo Airport</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ziro_Airport" title="Ziro Airport">Ziro Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Along_Airport" title="Along Airport">Along Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tezu_Airport" title="Tezu Airport">Tezu Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasighat_Airport" title="Pasighat Airport">Pasighat Airport</a> are small and are not in operation. The government has proposed to operationalise these airports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Before the state was connected by roads, these airstrips were originally used for the transportation of food.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parsuram.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="640" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Parsuram.jpg/220px-Parsuram.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Parsuram.jpg/330px-Parsuram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Parsuram.jpg/440px-Parsuram.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parsuram.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Road Tinsukia to Parashuram Kund in Arunachal Pradesh</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh has two highways: the 336 km National Highway 52, completed in 1998, which connects <a href="/wiki/Jonai" title="Jonai">Jonai</a> with Dirak,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and another highway, which connects <a href="/wiki/Tezpur" title="Tezpur">Tezpur</a> in Assam with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tawang_Town" title="Tawang Town">Tawang</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arunachal_Pradesh_State_Transport_Services" title="Arunachal Pradesh State Transport Services">Arunachal Pradesh State Transport Services</a> (or APSTS) is the state-owned road transport corporation. APSTS is running daily bus servicess from <a href="/wiki/Itanagar" title="Itanagar">Itanagar</a> to most district headquarters including <a href="/wiki/Tezpur" title="Tezpur">Tezpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guwahati" title="Guwahati">Guwahati</a> in <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shillong" title="Shillong">Shillong</a> in <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Dimapur" title="Dimapur">Dimapur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> As of 2007, every village has been connected by road thanks to funding provided by the central government. Every small town has its own bus station and daily bus services are available. All places are connected to <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>, which has increased trading activity. An additional National Highway is being constructed following the <a href="/wiki/Ledo_Road" title="Ledo Road">Stillwell Ledo Road</a>, which connects Ledo in Assam to Jairampur in Arunachal. Work on the ambitious 2,400 km two-lane <a href="/wiki/Trans-Arunachal_Highway" title="Trans-Arunachal Highway">Trans-Arunachal Highway</a> Project announced by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> on 31 January 2008 on his maiden visit to the state, was scheduled to be completed by 2015–16 but now due to political and social reasons it may take another decade.</p>
<p>In 2014, two major highways were proposed to be built in the state: <a href="/wiki/East-West_Industrial_Corridor_Highway,_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="East-West Industrial Corridor Highway, Arunachal Pradesh">East-West Industrial Corridor Highway, Arunachal Pradesh</a> in the lower foot hills of the state and 2,000-kilometre-long (1,200 mi) Mago-<a href="/wiki/Thingbu" title="Thingbu">Thingbu</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vijaynagar,_Changlang" title="Vijaynagar, Changlang">Vijaynagar</a> <a href="/wiki/Mago-Thingbu_to_Vijaynagar_Border_Road" title="Mago-Thingbu to Vijaynagar Border Road">Arunachal Pradesh Frontier Highway</a> along the <a href="/wiki/McMahon_Line" title="McMahon Line">McMahon Line</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR1-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR2_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR2-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR3_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR3-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR4_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR4-66">[66]</a></sup> alignment map of which can be seen here <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and here.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR5_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR5-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Arunachal Pradesh got its first railway line in late 2013 with the opening of the new link line from Harmuti on the main <a href="/wiki/Rangia-Murkongselek_section" title="Rangia-Murkongselek section">Rangpara North-Murkongselak railway line</a> to Naharlagun in Arunachal Pradesh. The construction of the 33 kilometre <span class="nowrap">1,676 mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">5 ft 6 in</span>) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_gauge" title="Indian gauge">broad gauge</a> railway line was completed in 2012, and the link became operational after the gauge conversion of the main line under <a href="/wiki/Project_Unigauge" title="Project Unigauge">Project Unigauge</a>. The state capital Itanagar was added to the Indian railway map on 12 April 2014 via the newly built 20 kilometre Harmuti-Naharlagun railway line, when a train from Dekargaon in <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> reached <a href="/wiki/Naharlagun_railway_station" title="Naharlagun railway station">Naharlagun railway station</a>, 10 kilometres from the centre of Itanagar, a total distance of 181 kilometres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 February 2015 the first through train was run from <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> to Naharlagun, flagged off from the capital by the Indian prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a>. India plans to eventually extend the railway to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tawang_Town" title="Tawang Town">Tawang</a>, near the border with China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arunachal_Pradesh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Education in Arunachal Pradesh">Education in Arunachal Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_institutions_of_higher_education_in_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="List of institutions of higher education in Arunachal Pradesh">List of institutions of higher education in Arunachal Pradesh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NERIST_academic_block.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="800" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/NERIST_academic_block.jpg/220px-NERIST_academic_block.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/NERIST_academic_block.jpg/330px-NERIST_academic_block.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/NERIST_academic_block.jpg/440px-NERIST_academic_block.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="612" data-file-width="816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG/220px-St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG/330px-St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG/440px-St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St_Claret_College_Ziro.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St Claret College Ziro</div>
</div>

<p>The state government is expanding the relatively underdeveloped education system with the assistance of NGOs like <a href="/wiki/Vivekananda_Kendra" title="Vivekananda Kendra">Vivekananda Kendra</a>, leading to a sharp improvement in the state's literacy rate. The main universities are the <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi_University" title="Rajiv Gandhi University">Rajiv Gandhi University</a> (formerly known as Arunachal University), <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Technological_and_Medical_Sciences_University" title="Indira Gandhi Technological and Medical Sciences University">Indira Gandhi Technological and Medical Sciences University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_University" title="Himalayan University">Himalayan University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> as well, together with nine affiliated Government Colleges as well as four private colleges. The first college, Jawaharlal Nehru College, Pasighat, was established in 1964. The First Technical University is Established in 2014 namely <a href="/wiki/North_East_Frontier_Technical_University_(NEFTU)" title="North East Frontier Technical University (NEFTU)">North East Frontier Technical University (NEFTU)</a>. In Aalo, West Siang District by The Automobile Society India, New Delhi. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Deemed_university" title="Deemed university">deemed university</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Regional_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="North Eastern Regional Institute of Science and Technology">North Eastern Regional Institute of Science and Technology</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Technology,_Arunachal_Pradesh" title="National Institute of Technology, Arunachal Pradesh">National Institute of Technology, Arunachal Pradesh</a>, established on 18 August 2010, is located in <a href="/wiki/Yupia" title="Yupia">Yupia</a> (headquarter of Itanagar).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> NERIST plays an important role in technical and management higher education. The directorate of technical education conducts examinations yearly so that students who qualify can continue on to higher studies in other states.</p>
<p>There are also trust institutes like Pali Vidyapith run by Buddhists. They teach Pali and <a href="/wiki/Khamti_language" title="Khamti language">Khamti</a> scripts in addition to typical education subjects. <a href="/wiki/Khamti_people" title="Khamti people">Khamti</a> is the only tribe in Arunachal Pradesh that has its own script. Libraries of scriptures are in a number of places in <a href="/wiki/Lohit_district" title="Lohit district">Lohit district</a>, the largest one being in <a href="/wiki/Chowkham" title="Chowkham">Chowkham</a>.</p>
<p>The state has two polytechnic institutes: Rajiv Gandhi Government Polytechnic in Itanagar established in 2002 and Tomi Polytechnic College in Basar established in 2006. There is one law college called Arunachal Law Academy at Itanagar. The College of Horticulture and Forestry is affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Central_Agricultural_University" title="Central Agricultural University">Central Agricultural University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imphal" title="Imphal">Imphal</a>.</p>
